Not sure why anyone needs 25 settings (as opposed to low, medium, high), but you'll probably do what I did, which is find a good temp for you, and leave it.<br /><br />BEWARE: This says it's a 1 1/4-inch brush, but it really means the barrel (the hot part) is 1 1/4-inches, and then there's the brush part, too, so it's more like 2+ inches in total. THAT is a substantial difference, if you have short hair. Long hair will be fine with it, but if your hair is shorter than 4 inches, this is pretty much going to straighten your hair, if you can even get it to engage at all.<br /><br />My hair is about 4 inches long in front, and longer in back, so I can wrap my hair around it easily in back, but the front hair barely stays with it, as I turn the brush. I have to hold it against the brush, as the &#34;bristles&#34; on the brush are not really brush-like at all. They're more like hard plastic pins, which keep the hot part away from your scalp, more than picking up and holding your hair. (Good for not tangling in the hair, but not so good for holding onto the hair.)<br /><br />This basically creates LARGE waves, more than curls, even on the longer hair. If that's what you want, fine, but know this is more of a straightener, than a curler. (I have really curly hair, so straightening is what I wanted it for, but I was intending for a smaller barrel, so my short hair would fit in it, too.)<br /><br />Overall, It works as intended, and heats up quickly. The cord is on one of those swivel cords, so you can turn it all day, and never tangle it, which I like. The cord length is good for bathroom sink outlets, with not too much excess to store when not in use.<br /><br />The big negative is the size error. When purchasing sight unseen, it is imperitive that size info be CLEAR and accurate. I knocked off a couple stars for that, and the ridiculous packaging, which forces you to destroy the package, so you can never return it. I'll eat this one, but I sure won't give it a good rating for a product which is nearly double the stated size.return it.   689. Blew out my electrical plug. I tried it on three different bathroom plugs and all stopped working.<br />&#34;A GFCI is much more subtle. When you look at a normal 120-volt outlet in the United States, there are two vertical slots and then a round hole centered below them. The left slot is slightly larger than the right. The left slot is called &#34;neutral,&#34; the right slot is called &#34;hot&#34; and the hole below them is called &#34;ground.&#34; If an appliance is working properly, all electricity that the appliance uses will flow from hot to neutral. A GFCI monitors the amount of current flowing from hot to neutral. If there is any imbalance, it trips the circuit. It is able to sense a mismatch as small as 4 or 5 milliamps, and it can react as quickly as one-thirtieth of a second.&#34;<br />This tells me the product came out of the box flawed. Maybe they have them made in China now, who knows? Anyway. Don't buy.
